Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
Two Methodological Commitments: Avoiding Speculative Theology and Sectarian Debates
Buti states his two commitments: avoiding discussion on divine attributes and avoiding extensive sectarian disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's two methodological commitments for writing his investigations: avoiding speculative theology on divine attributes and avoiding deep sectarian disputes.

Core Idea
Buti prioritizes essential faith over speculative theological debates.

In this passage, Buti lays out his methodology for the entire book. He wants to keep the focus on what is clear and essential for faith, avoiding discussions that lead nowhere or cause unnecessary sectarian divisions. This sets a pragmatic and focused tone for his theological approach.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the two commitments Buti lists.
2
Analyze the first commitment
Examine Buti's first commitment: refraining from debating the nature of divine attributes. Ask why he considers this futile.
3
Analyze the second commitment
Examine the second commitment: avoiding deep disputes with the Mu'tazila. Understand his justification that such disputes do not affect faith.
4
Synthesize the methodology
Consider how these two commitments together show Buti's focus on practical certainty and avoiding unnecessary theological speculation.
This will help you understand the overall approach of the book.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد التزمت الأمور التالية في كتابة هذه البحوث : أولاً ـ الابتعاد عن الخوض في حقيقة الصفات الإلهية وتحليلها وهل هي عين الذات أم غيرها ، وما يترتب على كل منهما ، مكتفياً باتباع مذهب جمهور المسلمين في ذلك . إذ يسع المسلم العاقل أن لا يفكر في ذلك أصلاً وأن لا يلتزم إلا ما نسبه الله تعالى إلى نفسه من صفات الكمال، على أنه لا توجد ثمة أي شبهة في الإيمان بالله يتوقف ردها على الخوض في هذا البحث الذي لا طائل فيه . ثانياً . عدم التوغل في كثير من الخلافات التي قامت بين المعتزلة وجمهور المسلمين من أهل السنة والجماعة ، إذ هي أمور لا ينتهي الجزم فيها بأحد القولين إلى الكفر ، لقيام الشبهة والاحتمال في أدلتها؛ ثم هي لا تتعلق بأي شبه في الإيمان لأي فئة من الناس اليوم . فحسبنا في ذلك أن نتبنى ما اتفق عليه جمهور المسلمين من أهل السنة والجماعة بعد معرفة الدليل والبرهان .
And I have committed to the following matters in writing these investigations: Firstly, refraining from delving into the reality of the divine attributes and their analysis, and whether they are identical to the essence or other than it, and what follows from each, contenting myself with following the school of the majority of Muslims in that. For the intelligent Muslim can avoid thinking about that entirely and not commit himself except to what God Almighty has attributed to Himself of attributes of perfection, on the basis that there is no doubt in faith in God whose rebuttal depends on delving into this futile research. Secondly, not penetrating deeply into many of the disputes that arose between the Mu'tazila and the majority of Muslims from Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, for they are matters in which being definitively certain of one of the two views does not reach disbelief, due to the existence of uncertainty and probability in their evidences; moreover, they are not related to any doubt in faith for any group of people today. So it suffices for us in that to adopt what the majority of Muslims from Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a have agreed upon after knowing the evidence and proof.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of two methodological commitments. The author states two principles he adhered to in writing. First, he refrains from discussing the metaphysical nature of divine attributes (whether they are identical to God's essence or distinct) and follows the majority view. He justifies this by saying that a reasonable Muslim can avoid these speculations entirely and only affirm what God has attributed to Himself, because no doubt in faith depends on resolving this issue, which he calls futile. Second, he avoids delving into the historical disputes between the Mu'tazila and the Sunni majority, because even being certain of one position does not lead to disbelief due to the presence of valid doubt and probability in the arguments. Moreover, these disputes are irrelevant to contemporary faith issues. He says it is sufficient to adopt the consensus of the majority after knowing the evidence. This shows his pragmatic approach to theology, focusing on practical certainty.

Key Terms
صفات إلهية
عين الذات
جمهور المسلمين
معتزلة
كفر
شبهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Buti is dismissing the importance of all theological debate.
Correction: He specifically avoids only the issues that are not essential to faith and have no definitive proof, not all theological debate.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why can the intelligent Muslim avoid debating the nature of divine attributes?
A) Because the arguments are too difficult.
B) Because no doubt in faith depends on resolving that issue.
C) Because the Mu'tazila have already settled it.
D) Because the Quran is silent on attributes.

Key Takeaway
Buti's methodology prioritizes clear and essential faith over speculative theological debates and sectarian disputes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter theological debates that seem endless and confusing, do you feel a pull to engage deeply or do you step back? Can you honestly say your faith depends on resolving these issues? What would it cost you today to follow Buti's path and focus only on what God has clearly revealed?
?
Think of a time you argued with someone over a religious matter that brought division rather than clarity. Was that argument necessary for your faith? If Buti's words 'لا طائل فيه' (futile) applied to that debate, how would you now choose to spend that energy instead?
?
You claim to believe in God's attributes of perfection—but do you live as if you truly believe, or do you spend more time analyzing them than embodying them? Buti says the intelligent Muslim can avoid thinking about the nature of attributes entirely. Honestly, compared to your intellectual curiosity, how strong is your desire for practical faith? What will you change today?

Method of Learning

Overview of the Book's Structure and Content
Author outlines the four main sections of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four-part structure of the book and the author's methodological approach starting from zero belief.

Core Idea
The author builds his case for Islamic belief starting from zero, using reason and science across four domains.

This passage is the author's own roadmap for the entire book. He clearly lays out the four major sections – divine matters, prophethoods, cosmic matters, and unseen matters – and explains his logical progression from one to the next. It's a bird's-eye view of the entire argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author states his plan in the first person.
This is a methodological outline, not a detailed argument.
2
Identify the four main sections
List the four areas: Ilahiyat (divine matters), Nubuwwat (prophethood), Kawniyyat (cosmic matters), Ghaybiyyat (unseen matters).
These are the book's major divisions.
3
Notice the starting point and method
The author says he starts from 'point zero in belief' using a scientific approach. This is key to his methodology.
He aims to convince both ancient and modern thinkers.
4
Examine the chronological sequence in Ghaybiyyat
Note that the unseen matters are listed in temporal order from portents of the Hour to Paradise and Hell.
This shows attention to detail and systematic presentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن أبدأ بالإلهيات ، فأعرض الدليل العلمي على وجود الخالق جل جلاله طبق المنهج الواضح في التمهيد بدءاً من نقطة الصفر في الاعتقاد ، بأسلوب يجمع بين إقناع قدامى المفكرين ومحدثيهم ، ثم أتحدث عن الصفات الإلهية بالتفصيل شارحاً ما يتعلق بكل منها مجيباً عن كل ما قد يرد عليها
ثم أتحدث عن النبوات : فأشرح معنى النبي والرسول ، وخصائص الأنبياء ، ولا بد من الإفاضة في البحث عند شرح ظاهرة الوحي وتحليلها ومعنى المعجزات وحقيقتها ، وموقف العقل والعلم من كل منهما .
فإذا انتقلت إلى البحث عن الكونيات ، تحدثت عن الإنسان والملائكة والجان وقانون السببية في الكون ، ولا بد من المقارنة عند ذلك بين حقيقة الإنسان وقصته كما يفصل القرآن فيها القول وكما ترى نظرية النشوء والتطور ، كما لا بد من التفصيل عند الحديث عن السببية والعلية في الكون تفصيلاً يجمع بين مقتضيات العلم وحاجة الإيضاح فإذا تحدثت عن الغيبيات ، بدأت بشرح معناها ، وذكرت القارئ بالمنهج العلمي للوصول إلى أمر يقيني بشأنها ، ثم أخذت أعددها الواحدة تلو الأخرى طبقاً للتسلسل الزمني ، أي بدءاً من أشراط الساعة ، فالموت ، فعذاب القبر ، فالحشر ، فالحساب فالميزان ، فالصراط ، فالجنة والنار ، راجياً أن يوفقني الله لحل كل مشكلة وردّ كل شبهة قد تعترض سبيل البحث العلمي في شيء من ذلك
And that I begin with the divine matters, so I present the scientific proof for the existence of the Creator, glorified be His Majesty, according to the clear methodology in the introduction starting from point zero in belief, in a style that combines convincing the ancient thinkers and the modern ones. Then I speak about the divine attributes in detail, explaining what pertains to each of them, answering everything that may be objected to them. Then I speak about prophethoods: so I explain the meaning of prophet and messenger, and the characteristics of the prophets, and it is necessary to elaborate in research when explaining the phenomenon of revelation and its analysis, and the meaning of miracles and their reality, and the stance of reason and science regarding each of them. Then when I move to the research about cosmic matters, I speak about humans, angels, jinn, and the law of causality in the universe, and it is necessary to compare at that point between the reality of humans and their story as the Qur'an details the statement therein and as the theory of evolution sees it, and it is also necessary to elaborate when speaking about causality and causation in the universe an elaboration that combines the requirements of science and the need for clarification. Then when I speak about the unseen matters, I begin by explaining their meaning, and I remind the reader of the scientific methodology to reach a certain matter regarding them, then I enumerate them one after another according to the chronological sequence, i.e., starting from the portents of the Hour, then death, then the torment of the grave, then the Resurrection, then the Reckoning, then the Scale, then the Path, then Paradise and Hell, hoping that Allah grants me success to solve every problem and refute every doubt that may obstruct the path of scientific research in any of that.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a methodological outline. The author states his plan to begin with the divine matters (ilahiyat), presenting a scientific proof for God's existence using a clear method starting from zero belief, appealing to both ancient and modern thinkers. Then he will detail the divine attributes. Next, he will address prophethoods (nubuwwat), explaining the meanings of prophet and messenger, their attributes, and analyzing revelation and miracles. Then he moves to cosmic matters (kawniyyat), discussing humans, angels, jinn, and causality, comparing the Qur'anic account with evolution. Finally, he will treat unseen matters (ghaybiyyat) chronologically: portents of the Hour, death, grave torment, Resurrection, Reckoning, Scale, Path, Paradise and Hell. He prays for success in solving problems and refuting doubts.

Key Terms
الإلهيات
النبوات
الكونيات
الغيبيات
السببية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is simply listing topics without a method.
Correction: The author emphasizes a scientific approach, starting from 'point zero in belief' and using reason to address both ancient and modern thinkers.

Checkpoint
What are the four main sections into which the author divides the book?
A) Ilahiyat, Nubuwwat, Kawniyyat, Ghaybiyyat
B) Tawhid, Nubuwwat, Akhirah, Qadar
C) Ilahiyat, Risalat, Akhlaq, Fatimat
D) Iman, Islam, Ihsan, Qiyamah

Key Takeaway
The book is structured into four sequential parts: divine matters, prophethoods, cosmic matters, and unseen matters, presented with a scientific methodology starting from zero belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to start your belief journey from 'point zero', setting aside all inherited assumptions? What would that require of you in your daily life?
?
The author uses science and reason to investigate even unseen matters. Do you approach your own beliefs with that same rigor, or do you rely on comfortable traditions? When have you last critically examined a core belief?
?
This lesson outlines a systematic plan for understanding faith. Do you have such a plan for your own learning? What would change if you committed to following a structured methodology like the author's?

Method of Learning
beginner

Third Methodology: Certainties and the Impartial Intellect
Author commits to avoiding non-definitive proofs and concludes with a prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's methodological commitment to rely only on definitive proofs and his exhortation to approach theological inquiry with an impartial intellect and scientific balance.

Core Idea
Certainties require a unique methodology: start from nothing and follow impartial reason.

In this passage, the author crystallizes his approach to the study of creed: he will only employ proofs that are definitive and certain, avoiding elaboration on matters lacking solid evidence. He then transitions into a heartfelt prayer and exhortation, urging both himself and the reader to adopt a neutral starting point and follow the path of reason alone, free from bias and desire. This sets the tone for his entire work.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the shift from methodological commitment to personal prayer.
The passage combines scholarly rigor with spiritual humility.
2
Identify the methodological commitment
Find the author's statement about not elaborating on matters without definitive proof. Understand why he restricts the book to certainties that are components of creed.
Key terms: دليل قطعي, برهان يقيني, مقومات العقيدة.
3
Reflect on the concluding prayer
Examine the prayer and exhortation. Note the emphasis on starting from 'the point of nothing', impartial reason, and avoiding partisanship. Consider the metaphor of life as a train speeding to death.
The prayer shows the author's reliance on God while advocating rational inquiry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً : عدم الإطناب في ذكر الأمور التي لم يثبت فيها دليل قطعي وبرهان يقيني ، بل لعلي لن أتعرض لكثير منها . إذ المجال هنا مختص بتلك الأمور التي قامت على القطع واليقين ، فكانت بذلك من مقومات العقيدة التي لا يسع المسلم إنكارها أو تجاهلها . ومن المعلوم أن لليقينات منهجاً مختصاً بها لا ينبغي أن يستبدل به غيره في سبيل الوصول إليها هذا وأسأل الله تعالى أن يوفقني ويوفق القارئ لدى البدء في قراءة هذا الكتاب إلى أن لا نلتزم إلا جادة العقل المنصف الحر وحدها ، وأن نتخلص من كل عصبية وغرض وشهوة ، وأن نبدأ كما قلت آنفاً من نقطة اللاشيء ثم نسير خطوة فخطوة على ضوء الميزان العلمي النزيه ، فأي نهاية أوصلنا إليها هذا السبيل ، وقفنا عندها والتزمنا التمسك بها . وإنه الجدير بمن كانت حياته قطاراً يمر به دون هدوء إلى الموت ، أن يبحث في تلك النهاية الغامضة وما وراءها وما يتعلق بها بحثاً متجرداً لا يقوم إلا على هدى العقل وحده . فما رأيت أغرب من مظهر رجل يمتطي ركوباً يغذ به السير إلى حيث لا يعلم ، وهو مع جذلان لا يحاول أن يسأل نفسه ولو في لحظة واحدة عن النهاية التي سينتهي إليها وعما عساه يستطيع أن يفعله من أجل ذلك ذلك مرح وعلى كل فأنا أكتب هذه البحوث لا أبتغي بها إلا الكشف عن الحقيقة ، ولا أبتغي على ذلك إلا مثوبة من خالق هذه الحقيقة ومكوّنها . وللقارئ أن يبتغي بعد ذلك ما يشاء
Third: Not elaborating on matters for which there is no definitive proof and certain evidence; rather, perhaps I will not address many of them. For the field here is specific to those matters that are based on certainty and conviction, and thus they are among the components of creed that a Muslim cannot deny or ignore. And it is known that certainties have a methodology specific to them that should not be replaced by any other in the way of reaching them. This, and I ask Allah Almighty to grant me success and to grant the reader success upon beginning to read this book to adhere only to the path of the impartial, free intellect alone, and to rid ourselves of every partisanship, ulterior motive, and desire, and that we start, as I said earlier, from the point of nothing, then proceed step by step in the light of the impartial scientific balance. So whichever end this path leads us to, we stop at it and commit to holding fast to it. And it is worthy for one whose life is a train passing quickly towards death to investigate that mysterious end and what is beyond it and what pertains to it, with an impartial investigation based only on the guidance of the intellect alone. For I have not seen anything stranger than the sight of a man riding a mount that speeds onward to where he does not know, while he is cheerful, not trying to ask himself even for a moment about the end he will reach and what he might be able to do for that. That is heedlessness. And in any case, I write these researches seeking only to uncover the truth, and I seek thereby nothing but reward from the Creator of this truth and its Maker. And after that, the reader may seek whatever he wishes.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is the third methodological commitment and a concluding exhortation. The author commits to avoiding elaboration on matters lacking definitive proof (dalil qat'i) and certain evidence (burhan yaqini). He restricts the book to certainties that constitute components of creed (muqawwimat al-'aqida) which a Muslim cannot deny. He notes that certainties have their own methodology that should not be substituted. Then he concludes with a prayer: he asks Allah to grant him and the reader success in adhering solely to the impartial free intellect, to abandon biases and desires, and to start from a neutral point (point of nothing) and proceed step by step with scientific balance. He emphasizes that one whose life is a train speeding to death should investigate the mysterious end and what lies beyond, using pure intellect. He criticizes those who ride heedlessly towards an unknown end without reflection. Finally, he declares his intention to seek only the truth and reward from God, and the reader may then seek what he wishes.

Key Terms
دليل قطعي
برهان يقيني
مقومات العقيدة
الميزان العلمي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the author rejects all theological reasoning or tradition.
Correction: The author is not rejecting all theological reasoning; he is insisting on using only certain evidence for creedal matters, and he combines this with prayer and reliance on God.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the proper methodology for reaching certainties?
A) Following the opinions of earlier scholars blindly
B) Using a specific methodology unique to certainties, starting from a neutral point and using impartial reason
C) Relying solely on transmitted texts without reason
D) Engaging in elaborate theological debates

Key Takeaway
The author commits to using only definitive proofs in theology and prays for the ability to follow impartial reason to discover truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author compares life to a train speeding towards death and criticizes the cheerful rider who never asks about his end. When was the last time you genuinely asked yourself about the end you are heading towards? Are you still that cheerful rider? Commit now to setting aside five minutes tomorrow to reflect on your final destination.
?
The author prays to be free from partisanship, ulterior motive, and desire. Which of these three do you struggle with most in your search for truth? What specific step will you take today to overcome it?
?
The author commits to starting from the point of nothing and following impartial reason. Are you willing to let go of your preconceived notions and biases to follow the truth wherever it leads, even if it challenges your comfort? How will you practice this starting tonight?

Method of Learning
beginner
5 min
Al-Būṭī’s Method: Certainty and Rational Inquiry
Al-Būṭī states his method: focus only on certainties and follow unbiased reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Būṭī’s methodological principles: focusing on certainties, using impartial reason starting from a neutral point, and the purpose of seeking truth.

Core Idea
Certainties demand their own method: impartial reason starting from nothing.

Al-Būṭī opens his work by laying down his method. He will only discuss matters of certain proof, and he calls for a fresh, unbiased rational approach. This passage sets the tone for a rigorous, evidence-based theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong emphasis on certainty and reason.
2
Identify key methodological principles
What does al-Būṭī say about the scope of the book? What does he say about the method for certainties? How does he describe the role of intellect?
Look for three parts: limitation to certainty, method of certainty, and the call to impartial reason.
3
Reflect on the 'point of nothingness' metaphor
Al-Būṭī proposes starting from 'the point of nothingness.' What does this mean in practice? How does it relate to freeing oneself from partisanship? Consider the train metaphor as well.
This is a powerful call to intellectual humility and openness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً - عدم الإطناب في ذكر الأمور التي لم يثبت فيها دليل قطعي وبرهان يقيني ، بل لعلي لن أتعرض لكثير منها . إذ المجال هنا مختص بتلك الأمور التي قامت على القطع واليقين ، فكانت بذلك من مقومات العقيدة التي لا يسع المسلم إنكارها أو تجاهلها . ومن المعلوم أن لليقينات منهجاً مختصاً بها لا ينبغي أن يستبدل به غيره في سبيل الوصول إليها هذا وأسأل الله تعالى أن يوفقني ويوفق القارئ لدى البدء في قراءة هذا الكتاب إلى أن لا نلتزم إلا جادة العقل المنصف الحر وحدها ، وأن نتخلص من كل عصبية وغرض وشهوة ، وأن نبدأ كما قلت آنفاً من نقطة اللاشيء ثم نسير خطوة فخطوة على ضوء الميزان العلمي النزيه ، فأي نهاية أوصلنا إليها هذا السبيل ، وقفنا عندها والتزمنا التمسك بها . وإنه الجدير بمن كانت حياته قطاراً يمر به دون هدوء إلى الموت ، أن يبحث في تلك النهاية الغامضة وما وراءها وما يتعلق بها بحثاً متجرداً لا يقوم إلا على هدى العقل وحده . فما رأيت أغرب من مظهر رجل يمتطي ركوباً يغذ به السير إلى حيث لا يعلم ، وهو مع جذلان لا يحاول أن يسأل نفسه ولو في لحظة واحدة عن النهاية التي سينتهي إليها وعما عساه يستطيع أن يفعله من أجل ذلك . وعلى كل فأنا أكتب هذه البحوث لا أبتغي بها إلا الكشف عن الحقيقة ، ولا أبتغي على ذلك إلا مثوبة من خالق هذه الحقيقة ومكوّنها . وللقارئ أن يبتغي بعد ذلك ما يشاء . غرة شوال : ۱۳۸۸ هـ - TV- ۲۷ - الدكتور محمد سعيد رمضان البوطي
Third: Avoiding elaboration on matters for which there is no definitive proof (dalīl qaṭʿī) and certain demonstration (burhān yaqīnī). Rather, I will not even address many of them. For the field here is restricted to those matters that are based on certainty (qaṭʿ) and certitude (yaqīn), and thus become components of the creed (ʿaqīda) that a Muslim cannot deny or ignore. And it is known that certainties (yaqīniyyāt) have their own particular methodology that should not be replaced by another in seeking to attain them. This, and I ask Allah Almighty to grant me and the reader, upon beginning to read this book, that we adhere only to the path of the impartial free intellect (ʿaql munṣif ḥurr), and that we free ourselves from every partisanship (ʿaṣabiyya), ulterior motive (gharaḍ), and passion (shahwa). And that we begin, as I said earlier, from the point of nothingness (nuqṭat al-lāshayʾ), then proceed step by step in the light of the impartial scientific balance (mīzān ʿilmī nazīh). So whatever end this path leads us to, we stop at it and commit to holding firmly to it. And it is befitting for one whose life is a train passing through him without rest toward death, that he investigate that obscure end and what lies beyond it and what pertains to it, in an objectified research that stands only on the guidance of intellect (hudā al-ʿaql) alone. For I have seen nothing stranger than the sight of a man mounting a ride that speeds him along to where he knows not, while being joyful, not attempting to ask himself even for a moment about the end toward which he is heading and what he might be able to do about it. And in any case, I write these researches seeking only the disclosure of truth (al-ḥaqīqa), and I seek no reward for that except from the Creator of this truth and its Maker. After that, the reader may seek what he wishes. Beginning of Shawwal 1388 AH. - 27 - Dr. Muhammad Saʿīd Ramaḍān al-Būṭī.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is from the author's introduction, outlining his methodological approach in writing the book. He begins by stating his third point: he will avoid discussing matters that lack definitive proof and certain demonstration. He clarifies that his focus is only on those issues that are established with certainty, as they form the indispensable components of Islamic creed that a Muslim cannot deny. He then emphasizes that certainties have their own specific method, which must not be substituted. The author then turns to prayer: he asks Allah to guide both himself and the reader to follow only the path of the free and impartial intellect, free from partisanship, ulterior motives, and passion. He advocates starting from a neutral point—'the point of nothingness'—and proceeding step by step using the objective scientific scale. Whatever conclusion this method yields must be accepted and adhered to. He then uses a powerful metaphor: life is like a train speeding toward death; one should reflect on the unknown end and what lies beyond, engaging in dispassionate inquiry guided solely by reason. He criticizes those who travel joyfully toward an unknown destination without questioning their fate. Finally, he declares his sincerity: he writes solely to uncover truth, seeking reward only from the Creator. The reader is free to seek whatever they wish thereafter. This sets the tone for a rational, evidence-based approach to theology.

The Necessity of a Knowledge-Based Method
Buti establishes the epistemological principle that knowledge requires a knowledge-based method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a knowledge-based method is necessary for attaining certainty and why conjecture cannot produce knowledge.

Core Idea
Knowledge only comes from knowledge, never from guesswork.

This passage from Buti sets up a foundational rule for all seekers of truth: the method we use to find reality must itself be reliable. He explains that knowledge can only arise from knowledge, not from conjecture. Before we compare Islamic and Western approaches, we must grasp this principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally before you interpret it.
Note that the passage ends mid-sentence; we focus on the complete argument presented.
2
Identify the key claim
The passage states that knowledge is only generated from knowledge like it. Find where this is stated and notice the logical consequence: conjecture cannot lead to certainty.
Look for the phrase 'العلم لا يتولد إلا عن علم مثله'.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Why does the author say that two conjectural premises producing a certain result is an impossibility? Consider how this shapes the requirement for a scientific method.
This connects to the learning objective about method and certainty.

Firstly
From the appendix
According to Muslim scholars and others
If the perception of reality as it is in actuality is knowledge, as they say, then the method adopted for that perception must - without doubt - also be knowledge, meaning that the steps of this method in its reality should be nothing but a set of truthful perceptions that would unveil the truth being investigated.
That is because knowledge is only generated from knowledge like it, and conjecture cannot at all be a path to knowledge. Otherwise, two conjectural premises could produce a certain result, and that is among the clearest cases of impossibility.
Hence, every seeker of truth must lay out for it a scientific method unsullied by intuition or fancy, and must adhere to this method, not deviating from it right or left.
That is an evident truth, about which no one should dispute.
But it is very possible that we ask: To what extent did Islamic thought and Western thought become aware of this truth and care for it?
Perhaps the word 'objective research' - that widespread, common word which among some people has become known for its association with Orientalist research - hastened to answer this question.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a methodological introduction. The author begins by stating a foundational epistemological principle: knowledge is the perception of reality as it truly is. Given that goal, the method used to attain such knowledge must itself be knowledge-based. That is, every step of the method must consist of truthful perceptions that gradually unveil the truth. The reason is that knowledge can only arise from knowledge; conjecture can never produce certainty. If it could, then two conjectural premises could yield a certain conclusion, which the author declares an impossibility. Therefore, any researcher must adopt a strictly scientific method, free from intuition or illusion, and follow it without deviation. The author asserts this as an undeniable truth. Then he transitions to a comparison: to what extent did Islamic and Western thought recognize and heed this principle? He suggests that the term 'objective research' - often associated with Orientalist studies - might provide an answer, but the passage breaks off before completing the point.

المنهج العلمي
الظن
اليقين
الحقيقة
الإدراك
الحدس
الوهم
البحث الموضوعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the author condemns all intuition, but he specifically rejects using intuition or fancy as a method for certainty, not intuition itself.
Correction: The passage states the method should be 'unsullied by intuition or fancy' (لا يشوبه الحدس أو الوهم), meaning that the method itself must be based on knowledge, not on subjective impressions. Intuition may have other uses, but it cannot be the foundation for a scientific method aimed at certainty.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Knowledge can only be built on knowledge; conjecture can never lead to certainty.

Knowledge Must Be Sought Through a Scientific Method
Buti defines knowledge and argues that its method must be certain, rejecting conjecture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti argues that the method for acquiring knowledge must itself be certain and free from conjecture.

Core Idea
Knowledge can only come from knowledge, never from conjecture.

Buti opens with a fundamental epistemological principle: if knowledge is the perception of reality as it is, then the method to reach that perception must also be certain. He then explains why conjecture can never lead to certainty. This lesson lays the groundwork for understanding the Islamic emphasis on rigorous methodology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the definition of knowledge and the condition that the method must be knowledge.
2
Identify the key argument
Find where Buti argues that knowledge only comes from knowledge, and why two conjectural premises cannot yield a certain conclusion.
This is the core logical move.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider what this means for the researcher: they must adopt a method free from intuition or illusion, and adhere strictly to it.
This sets the standard for scientific inquiry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولاً
من الملحقية
عند علماء المسلمين وغيرهم
إذا كان إدراك الحقيقة على ما هي عليه في الواقع، علماً، كما يقولون، فإن المنهج المتخذ إلى ذلك الإدراك ينبغي - بلا ريب - أن يكون هو الآخر علماً، أي ينبغي أن لا تكون خطوات هذا المنهج في حقيقته إلا مجموعة إدراكات صادقة من شأنها أن تكشف اللثام عن الحقيقة المبحوث عنها.
ذلك لأن العلم لا يتولد إلا عن علم مثله، وما كان للظن أن يصلح سبيلاً إلى العلم بحال، وإلا لأمكن لمقدمتين ظنيتين أن تأتيا بنتيجة يقينية وهو من أجلى صور المحالات.
من هنا، كان على كل باحث عن حقيقة أن يخط إليها منهجاً علمياً لا يشوبه الحدس أو الوهم. وأن يلتزم هذا المنهج لا ينحرف عنه يمنة ولا يسرة.
تلك حقيقة واضحة، لا ينبغي أن يتمارى فيها أحد من الناس.
ولكن من الممكن جداً أن نتساءل: ما مدى استشعار كل من الفكر الإسلامي والفكر الغربي بهذه الحقيقة واهتمامه بها؟
ربما أسرعت كلمة «البحث الموضوعي» تلك الكلمة الذائعة الشائعة، التي اشتهر بين بعض الناس ارتباطها ببحوث المستشرقين فحاولت الإجابة على هذا السؤال.
بيد أن الاعتماد على هذه الشهرة وحدها في إعطاء الحكم، سير إلى الحقيقة في منهج غوغائي غير علمي، لاجرم أنه يحرفنا عنها وإن أوهم أنه يوصلنا إليها. من الخير إذا أن نتلمس الجواب على هذا السؤال من واقع الطريقة التي يسلكها كل من علماء المسلمين وعلماء الغرب للوصول إلى حقيقة ما، سواء كانت معيارية (كما يقولون) أم تاريخية.
ولنبدأ بالطريقة التي ينتهجها الفكر الإسلامي.
وعلينا - قبل كل شيء - أن نقرر حقيقة ذات أهمية في هذا الصدد، وهي أن العامل الأول في إخضاع الفكر الإسلامي لمنهج علمي دقيق في البحث، كما سنجد، إنما هو الدين، وما كان للمسلمين - لولا العقيدة الدينية - أن يحملوا أنفسهم مؤونة منهج شاق يستنفد الكثير من الوقت والجهد دون أن يكون له حصيلة من كسب مادي معين، ثم يشتدون في التمسك به حتى يغدو مصطلحاً جميعاً يتعارفون به ويلتقون عليه.
ويتمثل هذا الدافع الديني في نصوص كثيرة من كتاب الله تعالى، من مثل قوله عز وجل: ﴿وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤَادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كَانَ عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً﴾ [الإسراء: ٣٦] وقوله عز وجل وهو ينعى على أقوام غامروا بعقولهم في متاهات من الأوهام والظنون التي من شأنها أن تغني على الحقائق ولا تكشف عنها: ﴿وَمَا يَتَّبِعُ أَكْثَرُهُمْ إِلاَّ ظَنّاً إِنَّ الظَّنَّ لا يُغْنِي مِنَ الْحَقِّ شَيْئاً إِنَّ اللَّهَ عَلِيمٌ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ﴾ [يونس: ٣٦].
وأنت ترى كيف يتمثل في هذا الدافع النهي عن تبني أي فكرة، حتى الدين نفسه، إلا عن طريق ما يثبته العقل الصافي من الدلائل اليقينية التي من شأنها أن تكشف عن حقيقة المطلوب.
First, from the supplement: According to Muslim scholars and others: If the perception of reality as it is in actuality is knowledge ('ilm), as they say, then the method (manhaj) taken to that perception should – without doubt – also be knowledge, i.e., the steps of this method in their reality should be nothing but a set of truthful perceptions that have the function of unveiling the reality under investigation. That is because knowledge is only generated from knowledge like itself, and conjecture (ẓann) can never be a proper means to knowledge at all; otherwise it would be possible for two conjectural premises to produce a certain result, which is among the clearest cases of impossibilities. Hence, it was incumbent upon every researcher of a reality to chart a scientific method free from intuition (ḥads) or illusion (wahm), and to adhere to this method without deviating from it right or left. That is a clear truth that no one should dispute. But it is very possible to ask: To what extent did Islamic thought and Western thought become aware of this truth and concern themselves with it? Perhaps the phrase "objective research" – that widespread and common phrase which some people associate with the research of Orientalists – hastened to answer this question. However, relying on this reputation alone in passing judgment is proceeding toward the truth in a demagogic, unscientific manner; undoubtedly it distorts us from it even if it gives the illusion that it leads us to it. It is better, then, to seek the answer to this question from the actual method that both Muslim scholars and Western scholars follow to reach some reality, whether it be normative (as they say) or historical. Let us begin with the method that Islamic thought follows. We must – before everything – establish a significant truth in this regard, namely that the primary factor in subjecting Islamic thought to a precise scientific method in research, as we will find, is indeed religion; and Muslims – were it not for religious creed – would not have burdened themselves with the hardship of a rigorous method that consumes much time and effort without yielding any particular material gain, and then hold fast to it until it becomes a common term they use and agree upon. This religious motive is embodied in many texts from the Book of God Almighty, such as His saying, Exalted be He: "And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge. Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart – each of those will be questioned" (Surah Al-Isra, 36), and His saying, Exalted be He, censuring people who risked their minds in labyrinths of illusions and conjectures that tend to obscure realities and not unveil them: "And most of them follow nothing but conjecture; indeed, conjecture does not avail against the truth at all. Indeed, God is Knowing of what they do" (Surah Yunus, 36). And you see how in this motive is embodied the prohibition of adopting any idea, even religion itself, except through what the pure intellect establishes of certain proofs that have the function of unveiling the truth of the sought object.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a methodological argument. Buti begins by defining knowledge as perception of reality as it is, and argues that the method to attain it must itself be knowledge, i.e., composed of truthful perceptions. He then states that knowledge only arises from knowledge, not conjecture, as two conjectural premises cannot yield certainty. Therefore, a researcher must adopt a scientific method free from intuition or illusion. Buti then poses a question: to what extent did Islamic and Western thought appreciate this? He warns against relying on the reputation of 'objective research' and instead proposes to examine actual methods. He begins with Islamic thought, asserting that the primary factor driving its rigorous method is religion, not material gain. He supports this with Quranic verses (17:36 and 10:36) that forbid following conjecture and command seeking certain knowledge. The passage concludes that this religious motive prohibits accepting any idea without certain proofs from the pure intellect.

Key Terms
علم
منهج
حقيقة
ظن
يقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any method is acceptable as long as the result seems plausible.
Correction: The passage argues that only a method built on certain knowledge can produce true knowledge; conjecture is insufficient.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why can't two conjectural premises produce a certain conclusion?
A) Because conjecture is always false
B) Because knowledge can only come from knowledge like itself
C) Because the method must be intuitive
D) Because the researcher may be biased

Key Takeaway
A scientific method must be built on certain knowledge, not conjecture, because knowledge only produces knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Reflect on a time when you held a strong belief about Islam simply because it 'felt right' or came from a respected person, without verifying its source. How does Buti's argument expose the danger of that approach, and what will you do differently from today?
?
Consider the last major religious question you settled in your mind. Did you build your conclusion on certain premises (from Quran, Sunnah, sound reasoning) or on speculation? Be honest. If on speculation, what is one step you can take this week to replace that shaky foundation with solid knowledge?
?
Buti says k nowledge only comes from knowledge. Where in your own life are you settling for conjecture instead of seeking certainty — not just in theology, but in your daily decisions? What is the cost of that comfort, and will you pay it?

The Religious Motive for Scientific Rigor in Islam
Buti explains the religious basis for Islamic methodology and cites Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti argues that religion, not material gain, drove Muslims to adopt a rigorous scientific methodology.

Core Idea
Religious creed motivated Muslims to pursue certain knowledge despite material costs.

After establishing the need for a certain method, Buti asks why Islamic thought embraced it so thoroughly. He asserts that the primary driver was religion, not worldly benefit. This lesson explores that claim and the Quranic verses that command believers to avoid conjecture and seek certainty.

Guided Path
1

2

Al-Isra 36 and Yunus 36.
3
Understand the conclusion

This ties the religious motive to the epistemological principle.

ولكن من الممكن جداً أن نتساءل: ما مدى استشعار كل من الفكر الإسلامي والفكر الغربي بهذه الحقيقة واهتمامه بها؟
ربما أسرعت كلمة «البحث الموضوعي» تلك الكلمة الذائعة الشائعة، التي اشتهر بين بعض الناس ارتباطها ببحوث المستشرقين فحاولت الإجابة على هذا السؤال.
بيد أن الاعتماد على هذه الشهرة وحدها في إعطاء الحكم، سير إلى الحقيقة في منهج غوغائي غير علمي، لاجرم أنه يحرفنا عنها وإن أوهم أنه يوصلنا إليها. من الخير إذا أن نتلمس الجواب على هذا السؤال من واقع الطريقة التي يسلكها كل من علماء المسلمين وعلماء الغرب للوصول إلى حقيقة ما، سواء كانت معيارية (كما يقولون) أم تاريخية.
ولنبدأ بالطريقة التي ينتهجها الفكر الإسلامي.
وعلينا - قبل كل شيء - أن نقرر حقيقة ذات أهمية في هذا الصدد، وهي أن العامل الأول في إخضاع الفكر الإسلامي لمنهج علمي دقيق في البحث، كما سنجد، إنما هو الدين، وما كان للمسلمين - لولا العقيدة الدينية - أن يحملوا أنفسهم مؤونة منهج شاق يستنفد الكثير من الوقت والجهد دون أن يكون له حصيلة من كسب مادي معين، ثم يشتدون في التمسك به حتى يغدو مصطلحاً جميعاً يتعارفون به ويلتقون عليه.
ويتمثل هذا الدافع الديني في نصوص كثيرة من كتاب الله تعالى، من مثل قوله عز وجل: ﴿وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤَادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كَانَ عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً﴾ [الإسراء: ٣٦] وقوله عز وجل وهو ينعى على أقوام غامروا بعقولهم في متاهات من الأوهام والظنون التي من شأنها أن تغني على الحقائق ولا تكشف عنها: ﴿وَمَا يَتَّبِعُ أَكْثَرُهُمْ إِلاَّ ظَنّاً إِنَّ الظَّنَّ لا يُغْنِي مِنَ الْحَقِّ شَيْئاً إِنَّ اللَّهَ عَلِيمٌ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ﴾ [يونس: ٣٦].
وأنت ترى كيف يتمثل في هذا الدافع النهي عن تبني أي فكرة، حتى الدين نفسه، إلا عن طريق ما يثبته العقل الصافي من الدلائل اليقينية التي من شأنها أن تكشف عن حقيقة المطلوب.
First, from the supplement: According to Muslim scholars and others: If the perception of reality as it is in actuality is knowledge ('ilm), as they say, then the method (manhaj) taken to that perception should – without doubt – also be knowledge, i.e., the steps of this method in their reality should be nothing but a set of truthful perceptions that have the function of unveiling the reality under investigation. That is because knowledge is only generated from knowledge like itself, and conjecture (ẓann) can never be a proper means to knowledge at all; otherwise it would be possible for two conjectural premises to produce a certain result, which is among the clearest cases of impossibilities. Hence, it was incumbent upon every researcher of a reality to chart a scientific method free from intuition (ḥads) or illusion (wahm), and to adhere to this method without deviating from it right or left. That is a clear truth that no one should dispute. But it is very possible to ask: To what extent did Islamic thought and Western thought become aware of this truth and concern themselves with it? Perhaps the phrase "objective research" – that widespread and common phrase which some people associate with the research of Orientalists – hastened to answer this question. However, relying on this reputation alone in passing judgment is proceeding toward the truth in a demagogic, unscientific manner; undoubtedly it distorts us from it even if it gives the illusion that it leads us to it. It is better, then, to seek the answer to this question from the actual method that both Muslim scholars and Western scholars follow to reach some reality, whether it be normative (as they say) or historical. Let us begin with the method that Islamic thought follows. We must – before everything – establish a significant truth in this regard, namely that the primary factor in subjecting Islamic thought to a precise scientific method in research, as we will find, is indeed religion; and Muslims – were it not for religious creed – would not have burdened themselves with the hardship of a rigorous method that consumes much time and effort without yielding any particular material gain, and then hold fast to it until it becomes a common term they use and agree upon. This religious motive is embodied in many texts from the Book of God Almighty, such as His saying, Exalted be He: "And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge. Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart – each of those will be questioned" (Surah Al-Isra, 36), and His saying, Exalted be He, censuring people who risked their minds in labyrinths of illusions and conjectures that tend to obscure realities and not unveil them: "And most of them follow nothing but conjecture; indeed, conjecture does not avail against the truth at all. Indeed, God is Knowing of what they do" (Surah Yunus, 36). And you see how in this motive is embodied the prohibition of adopting any idea, even religion itself, except through what the pure intellect establishes of certain proofs that have the function of unveiling the truth of the sought object.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a methodological argument. Buti begins by defining knowledge as perception of reality as it is, and argues that the method to attain it must itself be knowledge, i.e., composed of truthful perceptions. He then states that knowledge only arises from knowledge, not conjecture, as two conjectural premises cannot yield certainty. Therefore, a researcher must adopt a scientific method free from intuition or illusion. Buti then poses a question: to what extent did Islamic and Western thought appreciate this? He warns against relying on the reputation of 'objective research' and instead proposes to examine actual methods. He begins with Islamic thought, asserting that the primary factor driving its rigorous method is religion, not material gain. He supports this with Quranic verses (17:36 and 10:36) that forbid following conjecture and command seeking certain knowledge. The passage concludes that this religious motive prohibits accepting any idea without certain proofs from the pure intellect.

Key Terms
دين
عقل
ظن
حق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Islamic scholars were motivated by worldly gain or prestige.
Correction: Buti explicitly states that without religious creed, Muslims would not have undertaken the rigorous method, so the motive is religious.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what was the primary factor that caused Islamic thought to adopt a precise scientific method?
A) Material gain
B) Religion
C) Orientalist critiques
D) Greek philosophy

Key Takeaway
Islam's emphasis on certain knowledge and rejection of conjecture is rooted in religious texts, motivating a rigorous methodology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own pursuit of knowledge, are you more driven by the fear of being questioned about your hearing, sight, and heart on the Day of Judgment (as in al-Isra 36), or by the desire for worldly recognition or material gain? Which impulse actually shapes your study habits? Commit to one change this week: before accepting any significant piece of information, ask yourself whether you have certain knowledge of it as the Quran commands.
?
The passage states that without religious creed, Muslims would not have undertaken rigorous methodology. Look at your own approach to learning Islam: Are you willing to endure hardship for the sake of certain knowledge, or do you rely on convenient shortcuts and assumptions? What 'material gain' do you subconsciously prioritize over truth? Write down one area where you follow conjecture instead of certain proof and decide to investigate it.
?
You have been given the faculties of hearing, sight, and heart, all of which will be questioned. How will you account for the ideas you have accepted about your faith without verifying them through the pure intellect that Buti mentions? Is there a belief you hold about Islam that you have not subjected to this rigorous method? Resolve to study that topic with the same seriousness the Prophet's companions demonstrated.

Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
The Danger of Demagogic Methodology
Buti critiques reliance on popularity and introduces the need to examine Islamic methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why relying solely on popularity (shuhra) is considered a demagogic and unscientific approach in Islamic thought, and what alternative is proposed.

Core Idea
Popularity is not a path to truth; it can mislead rather than guide.

Buti begins his discussion by warning against a common pitfall: mistaking widespread acceptance for truth. He argues that relying on popularity alone leads to a demagogic methodology that distorts reality. Instead, one must look at the actual methods of scholars, starting with Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Notice the strong language (غوغائي, يحرفنا) that sets a critical tone.
The passage is short but packs a crucial warning.
2
Identify the critique of shuhra
Highlight the phrase 'منهج غوغائي غير علمي' and understand that 'shuhra' (popularity) is condemned as a false guide.
3
Understand the alternative
Buti proposes seeking the answer from the actual methods of Muslim and Western scholars, beginning with Islamic thought. This sets up the investigation.
Note the word 'نتلمس' – we are to seek, not assume.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيد أن الاعتماد على هذه الشهرة وحدها في إعطاء الحكم، سير إلى الحقيقة في منهج غوغائي غير علمي، لاجرم أنه يحرفنا عنها وإن أوهم أنه يوصلنا إليها. من الخير إذا أن نتلمس الجواب على هذا السؤال من واقع الطريقة التي يسلكها كل من علماء المسلمين وعلماء الغرب للوصول إلى حقيقة ما، سواء كانت معيارية (كما يقولون) أم تاريخية.

ولنبدأ بالطريقة التي ينتهجها الفكر الإسلامي.

وعلينا - قبل كل شيء - أن نقرر حقيقة ذات أهمية في هذا الصدد، وهي أن العامل الأول في إخضاع الفكر الإسلامي لمنهج علمي دقيق في البحث، كما سنجد، إنما هو الدين، وما كان للمسلمين - لولا العقيدة الدينية - أن يحملوا أنفسهم مؤونة منهج شاق يستنفد الكثير من الوقت والجهد دون أن يكون له حصيلة من كسب مادي معين، ثم يشتدون في التمسك به حتى يغدو مصطلحاً يتعارفون به ويلتقون عليه. ويتمثل هذا الدافع الديني في نصوص كثيرة من كتاب الله تعالى، من مثل قوله عز وجل: {وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤَادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كَانَ عَنْهُ مَسْئُولاً} [الإسراء: ٣٦] وقوله عز وجل وهو ينعى على أقوام غامروا بعقولهم في متاهات من الأوهام والظنون التي من شأنها أن تغني عن الحقائق ولا تكشف عنها: {وَمَا يَتَّبِعُ أَكْثَرُهُمْ إِلَّا ظَنًّا إِنَّ الظَّنَّ لَا يُغْنِي مِنَ الْحَقِّ شَيْئًا إِنَّ اللَّهَ عَلِيمٌ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ} [يونس: ٣٦]. وأنت ترى كيف يتمثل في هذا الدافع النهي عن تبني أي فكرة، حتى الدين نفسه، إلا عن طريق ما يثبته العقل الصافي من الدلائل اليقينية التي من شأنها أن تكشف عن حقيقة المطلوب.

ومن أجل هذا، قرر علماء التوحيد أن من شرط صحة إيمان المؤمن، أن يكون قائماً على دعائم من اليقين العلمي المجرد، لا على شوائب من التقليد والاتباع. وذلك لأن الحقيقة العلمية تعتبر - في حكم الدين - قمة المقدسات الفكرية وينبوعها. فهي التي ينبغي أن يحج إليها الفكر في خضوع وتطواف دائب. وهل من دليل على هذا الاعتبار أقوى من أن تجد الدين نفسه لا يرضى أن يقيم وجوده وقدسيته إلا على دعائم العلم وبراهينه، ولا يرضى أن يتخذ لنفسه حكماً من دونه؟ كل ما هنالك أن الإسلام أضفى الصفة الدينية على البحث عن الحقيقة بنبراس العلم والفكر المجردين، فإذا كان غير المسلم من شأنه أن يندفع إلى البحث برغبة حب التطلع، فإن المسلم مدفوع إلى البحث ذاته شعوراً منه بأنه واجب يثاب على فعله ويعاقب على تركه.

وهكذا وجد الفكر الإسلامي نفسه أمام مهمة دينية، هي ضرورة البحث عن الحقيقة، سواء أكانت من قبيل النقول أم الدعاوى. وبدهي أن القيام بهذه المهمة يتوقف على وضع منهج للبحث. ومعلوم أنه بقدر ما تكون الغاية صافية سليمة لا حكم فيها إلا للعقل وحده، يكون المنهج إليها صافياً سليماً أيضاً لا يخطه إلا العقل وحده.

ومع ذلك فنحن لا نكتب هذا البحث لنسرع فيه إلى الحكم بأن المنهج العلمي لدى المسلمين منهج سليم صاف لا تخطه إلا يد العقل وحده، وإنما الذي نقصد إليه هو البحث في هذا المنهج وسنصل إلى الحكم عليه في أعقاب ذلك.

(۱) نحن إنما نقصد بالدين - هنا - خصوص الإسلام، ومعلوم أن بين الإسلام والأديان الأخرى فروقاً كبيرة في هذا الصدد.
However, reliance solely on this popularity in giving judgment is a path to truth in a demagogic, unscientific methodology; it certainly diverts us from it even if it deludes that it leads us to it. It is better, therefore, that we seek the answer to this question from the actual method that both Muslim scholars and Western scholars follow to arrive at any truth, whether it be normative (as they say) or historical.

Let us begin with the method followed by Islamic thought.

We must - before everything - establish a fact of importance in this regard, namely that the primary factor in subjecting Islamic thought to a precise scientific method in research, as we shall find, is indeed religion; and Muslims would not have - without the religious creed - burdened themselves with the hardship of a method that consumes much time and effort without yielding any material gain, then they adhere strongly to it until it becomes a term they all recognize and agree upon. This religious motive is represented in many texts from the Book of God Almighty, such as His saying, Mighty and Majestic: {And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge. Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned about it} [Al-Isra: 36]; and His saying, Mighty and Majestic, as He reproaches people who risked their minds in mazes of illusions and conjectures that suffice over the truths and do not reveal them: {And most of them follow not except assumption. Indeed, assumption avails nothing against the truth. Indeed, God is Knowing of what they do} [Yunus: 36]. And you see how in this motive is embodied the prohibition of adopting any idea, even religion itself, except by way of what pure reason establishes from certain proofs that reveal the truth of what is sought.

For this reason, the scholars of tawḥīd (monotheism/harmonization) decided that among the conditions for the validity of a believer's faith is that it be based on pillars of abstract scientific certainty, not on blemishes of taqlīd (imitation) and following. That is because scientific truth is considered - in the judgment of religion - the pinnacle of intellectual sanctities and their source. It is that to which thought should make pilgrimage in submission and constant circumambulation. Is there any evidence for this esteem stronger than that you find religion itself not accepting to establish its existence and sanctity except on the pillars of knowledge and its proofs, and not accepting to take for itself a ruling without it? All that is that Islam conferred a religious character upon the search for truth by the lamp of pure science and thought; so if the non-Muslim is driven to research by the desire for curiosity, the Muslim is driven to the same research from his feeling that it is an obligation for which he is rewarded and for whose abandonment he is punished.

Thus, Islamic thought found itself before a religious task: the necessity of searching for truth, whether it be of the type of transmitted reports or claims. It is obvious that undertaking this task depends on establishing a method. And it is known that to the extent that the goal is pure and sound, with no arbitrator except reason alone, the method to it is also pure and sound, drawn by nothing but reason alone.

Nevertheless, we are not writing this research to hasten therein to the judgment that the scientific method among Muslims is a sound, pure method drawn only by the hand of reason alone. Rather, what we intend is to research this method, and we will reach a judgment upon it afterward.

(1) We only mean by religion - here - specifically Islam, and it is known that between Islam and other religions there are great differences in this regard.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an extended argument by Ramadān al-Būṭī on the religious foundation of the Islamic scientific method. He begins by critiquing reliance on popularity for judgment, calling it a demagogic and unscientific path that misleads. He then proposes to seek the answer from the actual methods used by both Muslim and Western scholars, intending to focus on the Islamic method.

The core argument is that religion itself was the primary factor that led Islamic thought to adopt a precise, rigorous scientific method. Without the religious creed (al-ʿaqīda al-dīniyya), Muslims would not have undertaken such a demanding method that required much time and effort with no material gain, and then adhered to it until it became a shared term. This religious motivation is exemplified in two Qur'anic verses: Surah al-Isra (17:36) which forbids following what one has no knowledge of, and Surah Yunus (10:36) which condemns following mere assumption (ẓann) that avails nothing against truth. These verses together establish the prohibition of adopting any idea—even religion itself—except through certain proofs (dalāʾil yaqīniyya) that pure reason (al-ʿaql al-ṣāfī) establishes to reveal the truth of what is sought.

From this, al-Būṭī states that the scholars of tawḥīd (ʿulamāʾ al-tawḥīd) made it a condition for the validity of a believer's faith that it be based on pillars of abstract scientific certainty (al-yaqīn al-ʿilmī al-mujarrad), not on the impurities of imitation (taqlīd) and following. The reason is that scientific truth is considered, in the judgment of religion, the pinnacle and source of intellectual sanctities; thought must make pilgrimage to it in submission and constant circumambulation. The strongest evidence for this regard is that religion itself does not accept to establish its existence and sanctity except on the pillars of knowledge and its proofs. Islam has given the search for truth a religious character, illuminated by the lamp of pure science and thought. The non-Muslim may be driven by curiosity, but the Muslim is driven by a sense of obligation—rewarded for performing it and punished for neglecting it.

Consequently, Islamic thought found itself facing a religious mission: the necessity of searching for truth, whether in transmitted reports (nuqūl) or claims (daʿāwā). This mission requires establishing a method. The purer and sounder the goal—with reason as the sole arbitrator—the purer and sounder the method, drawn only by reason.

Finally, al-Būṭī clarifies that he is not writing to rush to the judgment that the Islamic scientific method is purely rational and sound; rather, he aims to research the method and will reach a judgment after the investigation. A footnote specifies that by 'religion' here he means Islam specifically, noting significant differences from other religions in this regard.

Key Terms
الشهرة
المنهج الغوغائي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Widely held beliefs or popular opinions are a reliable guide to truth.
Correction: Buti argues that relying solely on popularity leads to an unscientific, demagogic method that diverts from truth rather than reaching it.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the problem with relying solely on 'shuhra' in giving judgment?
A) It is too slow to be practical.
B) It is a demagogic unscientific method that diverts from truth.
C) It requires too many people to agree.
D) It is acceptable only for historical matters.

Key Takeaway
Reliance on popularity alone is a false path; true methodology must be sought from the actual practices of scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek knowledge or make a judgment about a religious matter, how often do you check what the majority believes or what is popular among your social circle? How might that be misleading you about the truth? Commit to one change in how you verify information.
?
Buti says the demagogic method 'deludes that it leads us to it.' Have you ever been convinced you are on the right path solely because many around you agree? What would it cost you to examine the actual method of scholars instead of following the crowd? Write down a concrete step.
?
Think of a belief you hold strongly in Islam. Is it based on popularity among your peers or on a deep understanding of scholarly methodology? If you are honest, which weighs more? Resolve to investigate one such belief today using a reliable source.

Method of Learning
intermediate

The Religious Foundation of Islamic Scientific Methodology
Buti argues that religion was the primary factor in Islamic scientific method, citing Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how religious motivation was the primary factor that led Islamic thought to adopt a rigorous scientific method, as evidenced by Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Religion, not worldly gain, drove Muslims to develop a precise scientific methodology.

Buti now lays out a key fact: the main driving force behind Islamic scientific methodology was religion. Without religious creed, Muslims would not have endured the hardships of a demanding method with no material payoff. He supports this with Quranic verses that command pursuing knowledge based on certainty, not conjecture.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the religious motive
Read the Arabic and translation, noting Buti's emphatic statement that the primary factor is religion ('إنما هو الدين').
Pay attention to the phrase 'وما كان للمسلمين - لولا العقيدة الدينية - أن يحملوا أنفسهم مؤونة منهج شاق'.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
Read the two Quranic verses quoted: 17:36 and 10:36. Understand how they forbid following without knowledge and condemn mere assumption.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Buti concludes that adopting any idea, even religion, must be through certain proofs from pure reason. This links religious duty to rational certainty.

بيد أن الاعتماد على هذه الشهرة وحدها في إعطاء الحكم، سير إلى الحقيقة في منهج غوغائي غير علمي، لاجرم أنه يحرفنا عنها وإن أوهم أنه يوصلنا إليها. من الخير إذا أن نتلمس الجواب على هذا السؤال من واقع الطريقة التي يسلكها كل من علماء المسلمين وعلماء الغرب للوصول إلى حقيقة ما، سواء كانت معيارية (كما يقولون) أم تاريخية.

ولنبدأ بالطريقة التي ينتهجها الفكر الإسلامي.

وعلينا - قبل كل شيء - أن نقرر حقيقة ذات أهمية في هذا الصدد، وهي أن العامل الأول في إخضاع الفكر الإسلامي لمنهج علمي دقيق في البحث، كما سنجد، إنما هو الدين، وما كان للمسلمين - لولا العقيدة الدينية - أن يحملوا أنفسهم مؤونة منهج شاق يستنفد الكثير من الوقت والجهد دون أن يكون له حصيلة من كسب مادي معين، ثم يشتدون في التمسك به حتى يغدو مصطلحاً يتعارفون به ويلتقون عليه. ويتمثل هذا الدافع الديني في نصوص كثيرة من كتاب الله تعالى، من مثل قوله عز وجل: {وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤَادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كَانَ عَنْهُ مَسْئُولاً} [الإسراء: ٣٦] وقوله عز وجل وهو ينعى على أقوام غامروا بعقولهم في متاهات من الأوهام والظنون التي من شأنها أن تغني عن الحقائق ولا تكشف عنها: {وَمَا يَتَّبِعُ أَكْثَرُهُمْ إِلَّا ظَنًّا إِنَّ الظَّنَّ لَا يُغْنِي مِنَ الْحَقِّ شَيْئًا إِنَّ اللَّهَ عَلِيمٌ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ} [يونس: ٣٦]. وأنت ترى كيف يتمثل في هذا الدافع النهي عن تبني أي فكرة، حتى الدين نفسه، إلا عن طريق ما يثبته العقل الصافي من الدلائل اليقينية التي من شأنها أن تكشف عن حقيقة المطلوب.

ومن أجل هذا، قرر علماء التوحيد أن من شرط صحة إيمان المؤمن، أن يكون قائماً على دعائم من اليقين العلمي المجرد، لا على شوائب من التقليد والاتباع. وذلك لأن الحقيقة العلمية تعتبر - في حكم الدين - قمة المقدسات الفكرية وينبوعها. فهي التي ينبغي أن يحج إليها الفكر في خضوع وتطواف دائب. وهل من دليل على هذا الاعتبار أقوى من أن تجد الدين نفسه لا يرضى أن يقيم وجوده وقدسيته إلا على دعائم العلم وبراهينه، ولا يرضى أن يتخذ لنفسه حكماً من دونه؟ كل ما هنالك أن الإسلام أضفى الصفة الدينية على البحث عن الحقيقة بنبراس العلم والفكر المجردين، فإذا كان غير المسلم من شأنه أن يندفع إلى البحث برغبة حب التطلع، فإن المسلم مدفوع إلى البحث ذاته شعوراً منه بأنه واجب يثاب على فعله ويعاقب على تركه.

وهكذا وجد الفكر الإسلامي نفسه أمام مهمة دينية، هي ضرورة البحث عن الحقيقة، سواء أكانت من قبيل النقول أم الدعاوى. وبدهي أن القيام بهذه المهمة يتوقف على وضع منهج للبحث. ومعلوم أنه بقدر ما تكون الغاية صافية سليمة لا حكم فيها إلا للعقل وحده، يكون المنهج إليها صافياً سليماً أيضاً لا يخطه إلا العقل وحده.

ومع ذلك فنحن لا نكتب هذا البحث لنسرع فيه إلى الحكم بأن المنهج العلمي لدى المسلمين منهج سليم صاف لا تخطه إلا يد العقل وحده، وإنما الذي نقصد إليه هو البحث في هذا المنهج وسنصل إلى الحكم عليه في أعقاب ذلك.

(۱) نحن إنما نقصد بالدين - هنا - خصوص الإسلام، ومعلوم أن بين الإسلام والأديان الأخرى فروقاً كبيرة في هذا الصدد.
However, reliance solely on this popularity in giving judgment is a path to truth in a demagogic, unscientific methodology; it certainly diverts us from it even if it deludes that it leads us to it. It is better, therefore, that we seek the answer to this question from the actual method that both Muslim scholars and Western scholars follow to arrive at any truth, whether it be normative (as they say) or historical.

Let us begin with the method followed by Islamic thought.

We must - before everything - establish a fact of importance in this regard, namely that the primary factor in subjecting Islamic thought to a precise scientific method in research, as we shall find, is indeed religion; and Muslims would not have - without the religious creed - burdened themselves with the hardship of a method that consumes much time and effort without yielding any material gain, then they adhere strongly to it until it becomes a term they all recognize and agree upon. This religious motive is represented in many texts from the Book of God Almighty, such as His saying, Mighty and Majestic: {And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge. Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned about it} [Al-Isra: 36]; and His saying, Mighty and Majestic, as He reproaches people who risked their minds in mazes of illusions and conjectures that suffice over the truths and do not reveal them: {And most of them follow not except assumption. Indeed, assumption avails nothing against the truth. Indeed, God is Knowing of what they do} [Yunus: 36]. And you see how in this motive is embodied the prohibition of adopting any idea, even religion itself, except by way of what pure reason establishes from certain proofs that reveal the truth of what is sought.

For this reason, the scholars of tawḥīd (monotheism/harmonization) decided that among the conditions for the validity of a believer's faith is that it be based on pillars of abstract scientific certainty, not on blemishes of taqlīd (imitation) and following. That is because scientific truth is considered - in the judgment of religion - the pinnacle of intellectual sanctities and their source. It is that to which thought should make pilgrimage in submission and constant circumambulation. Is there any evidence for this esteem stronger than that you find religion itself not accepting to establish its existence and sanctity except on the pillars of knowledge and its proofs, and not accepting to take for itself a ruling without it? All that is that Islam conferred a religious character upon the search for truth by the lamp of pure science and thought; so if the non-Muslim is driven to research by the desire for curiosity, the Muslim is driven to the same research from his feeling that it is an obligation for which he is rewarded and for whose abandonment he is punished.

Thus, Islamic thought found itself before a religious task: the necessity of searching for truth, whether it be of the type of transmitted reports or claims. It is obvious that undertaking this task depends on establishing a method. And it is known that to the extent that the goal is pure and sound, with no arbitrator except reason alone, the method to it is also pure and sound, drawn by nothing but reason alone.

Nevertheless, we are not writing this research to hasten therein to the judgment that the scientific method among Muslims is a sound, pure method drawn only by the hand of reason alone. Rather, what we intend is to research this method, and we will reach a judgment upon it afterward.

(1) We only mean by religion - here - specifically Islam, and it is known that between Islam and other religions there are great differences in this regard.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an extended argument by Ramadān al-Būṭī on the religious foundation of the Islamic scientific method. He begins by critiquing reliance on popularity for judgment, calling it a demagogic and unscientific path that misleads. He then proposes to seek the answer from the actual methods used by both Muslim and Western scholars, intending to focus on the Islamic method.

The core argument is that religion itself was the primary factor that led Islamic thought to adopt a precise, rigorous scientific method. Without the religious creed (al-ʿaqīda al-dīniyya), Muslims would not have undertaken such a demanding method that required much time and effort with no material gain, and then adhered to it until it became a shared term. This religious motivation is exemplified in two Qur'anic verses: Surah al-Isra (17:36) which forbids following what one has no knowledge of, and Surah Yunus (10:36) which condemns following mere assumption (ẓann) that avails nothing against truth. These verses together establish the prohibition of adopting any idea—even religion itself—except through certain proofs (dalāʾil yaqīniyya) that pure reason (al-ʿaql al-ṣāfī) establishes to reveal the truth of what is sought.

From this, al-Būṭī states that the scholars of tawḥīd (ʿulamāʾ al-tawḥīd) made it a condition for the validity of a believer's faith that it be based on pillars of abstract scientific certainty (al-yaqīn al-ʿilmī al-mujarrad), not on the impurities of imitation (taqlīd) and following. The reason is that scientific truth is considered, in the judgment of religion, the pinnacle and source of intellectual sanctities; thought must make pilgrimage to it in submission and constant circumambulation. The strongest evidence for this regard is that religion itself does not accept to establish its existence and sanctity except on the pillars of knowledge and its proofs. Islam has given the search for truth a religious character, illuminated by the lamp of pure science and thought. The non-Muslim may be driven by curiosity, but the Muslim is driven by a sense of obligation—rewarded for performing it and punished for neglecting it.

Consequently, Islamic thought found itself facing a religious mission: the necessity of searching for truth, whether in transmitted reports (nuqūl) or claims (daʿāwā). This mission requires establishing a method. The purer and sounder the goal—with reason as the sole arbitrator—the purer and sounder the method, drawn only by reason.

Finally, al-Būṭī clarifies that he is not writing to rush to the judgment that the Islamic scientific method is purely rational and sound; rather, he aims to research the method and will reach a judgment after the investigation. A footnote specifies that by 'religion' here he means Islam specifically, noting significant differences from other religions in this regard.

Key Terms
العقيدة الدينية
العقل الصافي
الدلائل اليقينية
الظن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Islamic scholarly methodology was driven primarily by curiosity or material gain.
Correction: Buti states clearly that without the religious creed, Muslims would not have undertaken the strenuous method for no material gain; the motive was religious.

Checkpoint
What is the primary factor that led Islamic thought to adopt a precise scientific method, according to Buti?
A) Material gain
B) Curiosity
C) Religious creed
D) Philosophical tradition

Key Takeaway
The religious duty to seek truth with certainty, as commanded in the Quran, was the foundation of Islamic scientific methodology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a belief about your religion, do you ever stop to ask: 'Do I have a certain proof for this, or am I merely following what I was raised with?' How would you feel if you found out that you have been following assumption (ظن) in something that matters for your hereafter?
?
Think of the last time you sought knowledge—was it for worldly gain, or did you bear the hardship purely because God commanded you to seek truth? What would change in your approach if you truly internalized that your hearing, sight, and heart will be questioned about every piece of knowledge you pursue?
?
You have just read that the religious creed itself demands that you adopt no idea except through certain proofs. Is there any area of your faith where you have settled for less than certainty? What would it cost you to go back and build that certainty, even if it takes time and effort with no immediate material benefit?

Method of Learning
intermediate
7 min
Certain Knowledge: The Condition for Valid Faith
Buti explains the condition of faith based on certainty and the sanctity of truth, leading to a religious obligation of research.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Islamic scholars made certain knowledge (yaqin) a condition for valid faith, and how this elevated the search for truth to a religious obligation.

Core Idea
Faith must be built on certain knowledge, not imitation.

Building on the religious motive, Buti now draws an important conclusion: the scholars of tawhid established that a believer's faith must be based on abstract scientific certainty, not on imitation. This is because scientific truth is the pinnacle of intellectual sanctuaries in Islam. Consequently, the search for truth becomes a religious duty, and the method follows the purity of the goal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the condition of faith
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the key phrase 'دعائم من اليقين العلمي المجرد' and the contrast with 'شوائب من التقليد والاتباع'.
2
Understand the sanctity of truth
Buti describes scientific truth as the pinnacle of intellectual sanctuaries and uses the metaphor of pilgrimage (يحج إليها). Reflect on what this implies about the status of knowledge.
3
Trace the link to methodology
Buti argues that the method must be as pure as the goal. Since the goal is truth sought by reason alone, the method must be drawn by reason alone. Note the caveat that he is not prejudging the method.

Source Text

بيد أن الاعتماد على هذه الشهرة وحدها في إعطاء الحكم، سير إلى الحقيقة في منهج غوغائي غير علمي، لاجرم أنه يحرفنا عنها وإن أوهم أنه يوصلنا إليها. من الخير إذا أن نتلمس الجواب على هذا السؤال من واقع الطريقة التي يسلكها كل من علماء المسلمين وعلماء الغرب للوصول إلى حقيقة ما، سواء كانت معيارية (كما يقولون) أم تاريخية.
